           <a href="/wiki/Starfleet" title="Starfleet">
            Starfleet
           </a>
           <a href="/wiki/Admiral" title="Admiral">
            Admiral
           </a>
           <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Dougherty" title="Matthew Dougherty">
            Matthew Dougherty
           </a>
           in order to protect the
           <a href="/wiki/Ba%27ku" title="Ba'ku">
            Ba'ku
           </a>
           . (
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Insurrection" title="Star Trek: Insurrection">
             <span style="cursor: help;" title="Star Trek: Insurrection">
              Star Trek: Insurrection
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           )
          </dd>
          <dt>
           <a href="/wiki/2379" title="2379">
            2379
           </a>
          </dt>
          <dd>
           Travels to
           <a href="/wiki/Romulus" title="Romulus">
            Romulus
           </a>
           to meet
           <a href="/wiki/Praetor" title="Praetor">
            Praetor
           </a>
           <a href="/wiki/Shinzon" title="Shinzon">
            Shinzon
           </a>
           , a
           <a href="/wiki/Clone" title="Clone">
            clone
           </a>
           of himself; kills Shinzon during the battle with the
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Scimitar" title="Scimitar">
             Scimitar
            </a>
           </i>
           . (
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_Nemesis" title="Star Trek Nemesis">
             <span style="cursor: help;" title="Star Trek Nemesis">
              Star Trek Nemesis
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           )
          </dd>
         </dl>

         <h3>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Background_information">
           Background information
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Jean-Luc_Picard?action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit Background information section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h3>
         <figure class="article-thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://vignette2.wikia.nocookie.net/memoryalpha/images/8/8e/Picard_with_hair.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20130402225946&amp;path-prefix=en">
           <img alt="Picard with hair" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="Picard_with_hair.jpg" data-image-name="Picard with hair.jpg" data-src="http://vignette2.wikia.nocookie.net/memoryalpha/images/8/8e/Picard_with_hair.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/180?cb=20130402225946&amp;path-prefix=en" height="250" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Picard with hair" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="Picard_with_hair.jpg" data-image-name="Picard with hair.jpg" height="250" src="http://vignette2.wikia.nocookie.net/memoryalpha/images/8/8e/Picard_with_hair.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/180?cb=20130402225946&amp;path-prefix=en" width="180"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:Picard_with_hair.jpg">
           </a>
           <p class="caption">
            Stewart wears a hairpiece during a flashback sequence from "
            <a href="/wiki/Violations_(episode)" title="Violations (episode)">
             <span style="cursor: help;" title="Violations (TNG 5x12)">
              Violations
             </span>
            </a>
            "
           </p>
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <ul>
          <li>
           Picard was played by
           <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Stewart" title="Patrick Stewart">
            Patrick Stewart
           </a>
           in all of the character's television and film appearances.
           <a href="/wiki/David_Tristan_Birkin" title="David Tristan Birkin">
            David Tristan Birkin
           </a>
           played Picard as a child in
           <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation" title="Star Trek: The Next Generation">
            <span style="cursor: help;" title="Star Trek: The Next Generation">
             TNG
            </span>
           </a>
           : "
           <a href="/wiki/Rascals_(episode)" title="Rascals (episode)">
            <span style="cursor: help;" title="Rascals (TNG 6x07)">
             Rascals
            </span>
           </a>
           ", while
           <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Nash" title="Marcus Nash">
            Marcus Nash
           </a>
           appeared as Picard as a young
           <a href="/wiki/Ensign" title="Ensign">
            ensign
           </a>
           in "
           <a href="/wiki/Tapestry_(episode)" title="Tapestry (episode)">
            <span style="cursor: help;" title="Tapestry (TNG 6x15)">
             Tapestry
            </span>
           </a>
           ".
           <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hardy" title="Tom Hardy">
            Tom Hardy
           </a>
           was seen as Cadet Picard in a photograph in
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_Nemesis" title="Star Trek Nemesis">
             <span style="cursor: help;" title="???">
              Star Trek Nemesis
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           ; Hardy also played Picard's clone,
           <a href="/wiki/Shinzon" title="Shinzon">
            Shinzon
           </a>
           , in the same film.
          </li>
          <li>
           Jean-Luc Picard was the first character to be seen on
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation" title="Star Trek: The Next Generation">
             Star Trek: The Next Generation
            </a>
           </i>
           . Likewise, he was the last person to be seen in the final TNG outing,
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_Nemesis" title="Star Trek Nemesis">
             <span style="cursor: help;" title="???">
              Star Trek Nemesis
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           , (the second-to-last being a cameo).
          </li>
          <li>
           Other than in alternate realities, Jean-Luc Picard has always appeared as a captain, throughout the entire run of TNG and the subsequent movies. Data and Dr. Crusher are the only other characters to remain at the ranks they started with.
          </li>
          <li>
           The character of Jean-Luc Picard was named after Dr.
           <a class="extiw exitstitial" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Piccard" title="wikipedia:Jean Piccard">
            Jean-Felix Piccard
           </a>
           , a Swiss scientist, high-altitude balloonist, and member of a family of noted explorers. While there is no official source of the name Picard, the character makes occasional allusions to his "famous ancestors"  presumably Jean,
           <a class="extiw exitstitial" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auguste_Piccard" title="wikipedia:Auguste Piccard">
            Auguste
           </a>
           ,
           <a class="extiw exitstitial" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacques_Piccard" title="wikipedia:Jacques Piccard">
            Jacques
           </a>
           and
           <a class="extiw exitstitial" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bertrand_Piccard" title="wikipedia:Bertrand Piccard">
            Bertrand Piccard
           </a>
           .
           <ul>
            <li>
             Jean-Felix Piccard was the uncle of
             <a class="extiw exitstitial" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacques_Piccard" title="wikipedia:Jacques Piccard">
              Jacques Piccard
             </a>
             , who explored the Marianas Trench in 1960. Jacques Piccard's
             <a class="extiw exitstitial" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basthyscaphe" title="wikipedia:Basthyscaphe">
              Basthyscaphe
             </a>
             (deep sea submarine) was named
             <i>
              Trieste
             </i>
             , the potential namesake of the
             <a href="/wiki/USS_Trieste" title="USS Trieste">
              USS
              <i>
               Trieste
              </i>
             </a>
             .
            </li>
           </ul>
          </li>
          <li>
           It is also worth noting that a "Picard" is a sixteenth and seventeenth century term for someone of an enquiring mindset (derived from the birthplace of
           <a class="extiw exitstitial" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Calvin" title="wikipedia:John Calvin">
            John Calvin
           </a>
           of Picardy or Picardie). With his interest in the development of Humanism, it is likely Roddenberry knew this. Certainly it is a fitting description of Jean-Luc's character as well as his name.
          </li>
          <li>
           Further, there was a 17th-century Catholic priest and astronomer, named
           <a class="extiw exitstitial" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Picard" title="wikipedia:Jean Picard">
            Jean Picard
           </a>
           , who was the first to measure the Earth's size to a high degree of accuracy, and who kept close contacts with
           <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">
            Isaac Newton
           </a>
           and
           <a class="extiw exitstitial" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tycho_Brahe" title="wikipedia:Tycho Brahe">
            Tycho Brahe
           </a>
           , who may have also contributed to the character's naming.
          </li>
          <li>
           The original casting call sent out to agents asked for the following:
          </li>
         </ul>
         <dl>
          <dd>
           <dl>
            <dd>
             <i>
              CAPT. Julien Picard  A Caucasian man in his 50s who is very youthful and in prime physical condition. Born in
              <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">
               Paris
              </a>
              , his Gallic accent appears when deep emotions are triggered. He is definitely a "romantic" and believes strongly in concepts like honor and duty. Capt. Picard commands the
             </i>
             Enterprise
             <i>
              . He should have a mid-Atlantic accent, and a wonderfully rich speaking voice.
             </i>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </dd>
         </dl>
         <ul>
          <li>
           Picard was most popular for straightening his uniform when standing up (the "Picard Maneuver", different from the tactical maneuver he first performed with the
           <i>
            Stargazer
           </i>
           ), saying "
           <i>
            Engage
           </i>
           " after plotting a course, and "
           <i>
            Make it so
           </i>
           " when agreeing with someone's suggested orders.
          </li>
          <li>
           In recent years, several popular
           <a class="extiw exitstitial" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_meme" title="wikipedia:Internet meme">
            Internet memes
           </a>
           have surfaced in connection with Picard, most notably the "Picard facepalm" (originally based on a scene from "
           <a href="/wiki/Deja_Q_(episode)" title="Deja Q (episode)">
            <span style="cursor: help;" title="???">
             Deja Q
            </span>
           </a>
           "), and its numerous derivatives.
           <a class="external autonumber exitstitial" href="http://knowyourmeme.com/memes/people/jean-luc-picard" rel="nofollow">
            [2]
           </a>
          </li>
          <li>
           There are a number of musical tributes to Picard, most notably DarkMateria's "Picard Song Tribute"
           <a class="external autonumber exitstitial" href="http://tborgax.homepage.dk/audio.html" rel="nofollow">
            [3]
           </a>
           and Bryan Erickson's "Futile".
           <a class="external autonumber exitstitial" href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B00000IKVD/103-2727187-4719053?v=glance&amp;n=5174&amp;colid=&amp;coliid=" rel="nofollow">
            [4]
           </a>
          </li>
          <li>
           The character of Picard changed quite a bit from the original March, 1987 Writers/Directors guide. In that guide, he was born in Paris, carried a touch of French phrasing in his speech, and pretended that France is "the only true civilization" on
           <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">
            Earth
           </a>
           (reminiscent of
           <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Chekov" title="Pavel Chekov">
            Pavel Chekov
           </a>
           ). The latter only  surfaced briefly in some early episodes (most notably "
           <a href="/wiki/The_Last_Outpost_(episode)" title="The Last Outpost (episode)">
            <span style="cursor: help;" title="???">
             The Last Outpost
            </span>
           </a>
           "). Over the course of the series, his character became more English. He enjoyed the works of
           <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">
            William Shakespeare
           </a>
           , and was never seen reading a French author. He drinks
           <a href="/wiki/Earl_Grey_tea" title="Earl Grey tea">
            Earl Grey tea
           </a>
           , an English beverage named after an English nobleman, and was rarely seen drinking wine (he only drinks it on three occasions, once in "
           <a href="/wiki/First_Contact_(episode)" title="First Contact (episode)">
            <span style="cursor: help;" title="???">
             First Contact
            </span>
           </a>
           ", again in "
           <a href="/wiki/Family_(episode)" title="Family (episode)">
            <span style="cursor: help;" title="???">
             Family
            </span>
           </a>
           ", and once at the end of
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_Nemesis" title="Star Trek Nemesis">
             <span style="cursor: help;" title="???">
              Star Trek Nemesis
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           ), a beverage which is commonplace in French life. Additionally, his brother and nephew both spoke with English accents.
          </li>
          <li>
           Picard was originally intended to be in his early 50s, with a 22-year stint captaining the
           <i>
            Stargazer
           </i>
           ; Stewart himself was 47 in 1987. The show established a long gap between the
           <i>
            Stargazer
           </i>
           and the
           <i>
            Enterprise
           </i>
           -D; the Okuda timeline states he was 59 in TNG season 1 (and thus is 74 in
           <i>
            Star Trek Nemesis
           </i>
           , compared to Stewart's 62).
          </li>
          <li>
           Picard has the distinction of having on-screen dialog with three of the four other main
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek" title="Star Trek">
             Star Trek
            </a>
           </i>
           captains, the most by any other captain. Picard met with
           <a href="/wiki/James_T._Kirk" title="James T. Kirk">
            James T. Kirk
           </a>
           in the movie
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_Generations" title="Star Trek Generations">
             <span style="cursor: help;" title="???">
              Star Trek Generations
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           ,
           <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Sisko" title="Benjamin Sisko">
            Benjamin Sisko
           </a>
           in the
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DS9" title="DS9">
            DS9
           </a>
           pilot, "
           <a href="/wiki/Emissary_(episode)" title="Emissary (episode)">
            <span style="cursor: help;" title="???">
             Emissary
            </span>
           </a>
           ", and
           <a href="/wiki/Kathryn_Janeway" title="Kathryn Janeway">
            Kathryn Janeway
           </a>
           in the movie
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_Nemesis" title="Star Trek Nemesis">
             <span style="cursor: help;" title="???">
              Star Trek Nemesis
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           (although in this last instance, they communicated over a viewscreen without actually meeting face-to-face). He has not had any on-screen dialog with
           <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Archer" title="Jonathan Archer">
            Jonathan Archer
           </a>
           .
          </li>
          <li>
           During an interview with
           <a class="extiw exitstitial" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Parkinson" title="wikipedia:Michael Parkinson">
            Michael Parkinson
           </a>
           , Patrick Stewart related how in his first press conference for
           <i>
            The Next Generation
           </i>
           , a reporter asked
           <a href="/wiki/Gene_Roddenberry" title="Gene Roddenberry">
            Gene Roddenberry
           </a>
           how Captain Picard could be bald, figuring that baldness would surely be cured by the
           <a href="/wiki/24th_century" title="24th century">
            24th century
           </a>
           . Roddenberry replied that "by the 24th century, no one will care."
           <a class="external autonumber exitstitial" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pXOK-ZVJMaU" rel="nofollow">
            [5]
           </a>
          </li>
          <li>
           Picard is one of five characters to appear in two series premieres (
           <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation" title="Star Trek: The Next Generation">
            <span style="cursor: help;" title="Star Trek: The Next Generation">
             TNG
            </span>
           </a>
           : "
           <a href="/wiki/Encounter_at_Farpoint_(episode)" title="Encounter at Farpoint (episode)">
            <span style="cursor: help;" title="???">
             Encounter at Farpoint
            </span>
           </a>
           " and
           <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Deep_Space_Nine" title="Star Trek: Deep Space Nine">
            <span style="cursor: help;" title="Star Trek: Deep Space Nine">
             DS9
            </span>
           </a>
           : "
           <a href="/wiki/Emissary_(episode)" title="Emissary (episode)">
            <span style="cursor: help;" title="???">
             Emissary
            </span>
           </a>
           "), the others being
           <a href="/wiki/Miles_O%27Brien" title="Miles O'Brien">
            Miles O'Brien
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="/wiki/Quark" title="Quark">
            Quark
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="/wiki/Broik" title="Broik">
            Broik
           </a>
           and
           <a href="/wiki/Morn" title="Morn">
            Morn
           </a>
           .  He also has the distinction of having spoken the first lines of dialog in both series, and was the first character seen on screen in both (albeit in the form of Locutus on the latter).
          </li>
          <li>
           Apart from
           <a href="/wiki/James_T._Kirk" title="James T. Kirk">
            James T. Kirk
           </a>
           , Picard is the only person to captain two
           <i>
            Enterprise
           </i>
           s, commanding the
           <a href="/wiki/USS_Enterprise_(NCC-1701-D)" title="USS Enterprise (NCC-1701-D)">
            USS
            <i>
             Enterprise
            </i>
            -D
           </a>
           and the
           <a href="/wiki/USS_Enterprise_(NCC-1701-E)" title="USS Enterprise (NCC-1701-E)">
            USS
            <i>
             Enterprise
            </i>
            -E
           </a>
           . With the restoration of a cut scene from the extended version of the episode "
           <a href="/wiki/The_Measure_Of_A_Man_(episode)" title="The Measure Of A Man (episode)">
            <span style="cursor: help;" title="???">
             The Measure Of A Man
            </span>
           </a>
           " (thus making the scene
           <a href="/wiki/Canon" title="Canon">
            canon
           </a>
           ), Picard also shares with
           <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Chekov" title="Pavel Chekov">
            Pavel Chekov
           </a>
           the distinction of having served aboard two starships name
           <i>
            Enterprise
           </i>
           and one named
           <a href="/wiki/USS_Reliant_(24th_century)" title="USS Reliant (24th century)">
            USS
            <i>
             Reliant
            </i>
           </a>
           .
          </li>
          <li>
           Picard is the only lead character in any
           <i>
            Star Trek
           </i>
           production who was not
           <a href="/wiki/American" title="American">
            American
           </a>
           .
           <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Archer" title="Jonathan Archer">
            Jonathan Archer
           </a>
           was born in upstate
           <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">
            New York
           </a>
           and raised in
           <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">
            San Francisco
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
            California
           </a>
           ;
           <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Pike" title="Christopher Pike">
            Christopher Pike
           </a>
           was born in
           <a href="/wiki/Mojave" title="Mojave">
            Mojave
           </a>
           , California;
           <a href="/wiki/James_T._Kirk" title="James T. Kirk">
            James T. Kirk
           </a>
           was from
           <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">
            Iowa
           </a>
           , (his
           <a href="/wiki/James_T._Kirk_(alternate_reality)" title="James T. Kirk (alternate reality)">
            alternate reality counterpart
           </a>
           was born in space, but apparently still raised there, as well);
           <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Sisko" title="Benjamin Sisko">
            Benjamin Sisko
           </a>
           was born in
           <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">
            New Orleans
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">
            Louisiana
           </a>
           ; and
           <a href="/wiki/Kathryn_Janeway" title="Kathryn Janeway">
            Kathryn Janeway
           </a>
           was born in
           <a href="/wiki/Bloomington" title="Bloomington">
            Bloomington
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">
            Indiana
           </a>
           .
          </li>
          <li>
           In an
           <a class="external text exitstitial" href="http://www.npr.org/2014/12/13/370331835/not-my-job-actor-patrick-stewart-gets-quizzed-on-g-i-joe" rel="nofollow">
            2014 appearance
           </a>
           on
           <a class="extiw exitstitial" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NPR" title="wikipedia:NPR">
            NPR
           </a>
           's quiz show
           <i>
            <a class="extiw exitstitial" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wait,_Wait..._Don%27t_Tell_Me!" title="wikipedia:Wait, Wait... Don't Tell Me!">
             Wait, Wait... Don't Tell Me!
            </a>
           </i>
           , Patrick Stewart indicated that the real life reason for Picard lacking a French accent was that it sounded silly when he attempted it:
          </li>
         </ul>
         <dl>
          <dd>
           <dl>
            <dd>
             "
             <i>
              Yes, you know, I did somewhere in the bowels of
              <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">
               Paramount Pictures
              </a>
              , there - I hope it still exists - there is a recording of me on camera playing Captain Picard - some of the scenes from the pilot episode with a French accent. ... If he was a Frenchman, why shouldn't he have a French accent? And, I mean, can you imagine it?
             </i>
             (imitating French accent)
             <i>
              Space, ze final frontier.
             </i>
             (applause)
             <i>
              It would not have worked. I have a great respect for the French and certainly I adore the French language, but no. It would not have worked. I doubt I would have sounded more like Inspector Clouseau.
             </i>
             "
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </dd>
         </dl>
         <h3>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Apocrypha">
           Apocrypha
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Jean-Luc_Picard?action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit Apocrypha section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h3>
         <figure class="article-thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://vignette1.wikia.nocookie.net/memoryalpha/images/9/92/Countdown_Picard.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20090617195724&amp;path-prefix=en">
           <img alt="Countdown Picard" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="Countdown_Picard.jpg" data-image-name="Countdown Picard.jpg" data-src="http://vignette1.wikia.nocookie.net/memoryalpha/images/9/92/Countdown_Picard.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/180?cb=20090617195724&amp;path-prefix=en" height="250" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Countdown Picard" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="Countdown_Picard.jpg" data-image-name="Countdown Picard.jpg" height="250" src="http://vignette1.wikia.nocookie.net/memoryalpha/images/9/92/Countdown_Picard.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/180?cb=20090617195724&amp;path-prefix=en" width="180"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:Countdown_Picard.jpg">
           </a>
           <p class="caption">
            Picard in
            <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Countdown" title="Star Trek: Countdown">
             Star Trek: Countdown
            </a>
           </p>
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <ul>
          <li>
           In the alternate future of the
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DS9" title="DS9">
            DS9
           </a>
           book series
           <i>
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Millennium" title="Millennium">
             Millennium
            </a>
           </i>
           , Picard was
           <a href="/wiki/Captain" title="Captain">
            captain
           </a>
           of the
           <a href="/wiki/USS_Enterprise_(NCC-1701-E)" title="USS Enterprise (NCC-1701-E)">
            USS
            <i>
             Enterprise
            </i>
            -E
           </a>
           . He took
           <a href="/wiki/Ensign" title="Ensign">
            Ensign
           </a>
           <a href="/wiki/Nog" title="Nog">
            Nog
           </a>
           under his wing after Nog was assigned to the
           <i>
            Enterprise
           </i>
           . On
           <a href="/wiki/Stardate" title="Stardate">
            stardate
           </a>
           52145.7, Picard attempted to intercept a
           <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">
            Dominion
           </a>
           warship carrying
           <a href="/wiki/Weyoun" title="Weyoun">
            Weyoun
           </a>
           . However, Weyoun escaped into the
           <a href="/wiki/Pah-wraith" title="Pah-wraith">
            Pah-wraith
           </a>
           <a href="/wiki/Wormhole" title="Wormhole">
            wormhole
           </a>
           . In 2381, the
           <i>
            Enterprise
           </i>
           was destroyed at the Battle of Rigel VII. According to
           <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Riker" title="Thomas Riker">
            Thomas Riker
           </a>
           , a Starfleet hearing was called, since Picard had lost his third ship (the
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/USS_Stargazer" title="USS Stargazer">
             Stargazer
            </a>
           </i>
           ,
           <a href="/wiki/USS_Enterprise_(NCC-1701-D)" title="USS Enterprise (NCC-1701-D)">
            USS
            <i>
             Enterprise
            </i>
            -D
           </a>
           , and
           <i>
            Enterprise
           </i>
           -E), but the case was dismissed and Picard was given command of the
           <i>
            Enterprise
           </i>
           -F in 2383, described as the "first of its class." In 2385, Picard accepted a promotion to
           <a href="/wiki/Admiral" title="Admiral">
            admiral
           </a>
           , and
           <a href="/wiki/William_T._Riker" title="William T. Riker">
            William T. Riker
           </a>
           was given command of the
           <i>
            Enterprise
           </i>
           . When
           <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">
            Earth
           </a>
           was destroyed by the Grigari, Picard survived. By 2399, Picard was stricken with
           <a href="/wiki/Irumodic_Syndrome" title="Irumodic Syndrome">
            Irumodic Syndrome
           </a>
           , and would occasionally do such things as speak to nobody (although he claimed to be speaking to
           <a href="/wiki/Q" title="Q">
            Q
           </a>
           ), or mistake other officers for his old crew (for example, he called Nog "Will" and Jake "
           <a href="/wiki/Geordi_La_Forge" title="Geordi La Forge">
            Geordi
           </a>
           "). It is implied that he married
           <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Crusher" title="Beverly Crusher">
            Beverly Crusher
           </a>
           , as he comments to
           <a href="/wiki/Julian_Bashir" title="Julian Bashir">
            Julian Bashir
           </a>
           that, between Bashir and
           <a href="/wiki/Leonard_McCoy" title="Leonard McCoy">
            Leonard McCoy
           </a>
           , he was always worried that his wife would leave him for one of her heroes. Picard headed up a task force to build a
           <a href="/wiki/Timeship" title="Timeship">
            timeship
           </a>
           known as the USS
           <i>
            Phoenix
           </i>
           to try and undo the timeline. However, the
           <i>
            Phoenix
           </i>
           was destroyed before it could accomplish its mission, but Picard, Nog, and
           <a href="/wiki/Vash" title="Vash">
            Vash
           </a>
           traveled back in time twenty-five thousand years, where they became three
           <a href="/wiki/Bajoran" title="Bajoran">
            Bajoran
           </a>
           mystics who wrote prophecies of the events they had experienced; it is also implied that Vash and the elder Picard were married. The entire timeline was later reset thanks to the actions of
           <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Sisko" title="Benjamin Sisko">
            Benjamin Sisko
           </a>
           .
          </li>
          <li>
           The novel
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Death_in_Winter" title="Death in Winter">
             Death in Winter
            </a>
           </i>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jan_Friedman" title="Michael Jan Friedman">
            Michael Jan Friedman
           </a>
           told of Picard beginning a romantic relationship with Dr. Beverly Crusher after rescuing her from a planet under Romulan control. A subsequent book,
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Greater_than_the_Sum" title="Greater than the Sum">
             Greater than the Sum
            </a>
           </i>
           , by
           <a class="new" href="/wiki/Christopher_Bennett?action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Christopher Bennett (page does not exist)">
            Christopher Bennett
           </a>
           , portrayed them as married and expecting a child. The later
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Paths_of_Disharmony" title="Paths of Disharmony">
             Paths of Disharmony
            </a>
           </i>
           , by
           <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Ward" title="Dayton Ward">
            Dayton Ward
           </a>
           , shows them with a son, Ren.
          </li>
          <li>
           The graphic novel
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/The_Gorn_Crisis" title="The Gorn Crisis">
             The Gorn Crisis
            </a>
           </i>
           showed Picard undertaking a mission during the
           <a href="/wiki/Dominion_War" title="Dominion War">
            Dominion War
           </a>
           to make an alliance with the
           <a href="/wiki/Gorn" title="Gorn">
            Gorn
           </a>
           .
          </li>
          <li>
           The comic book series
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Countdown" title="Star Trek: Countdown">
             Star Trek: Countdown
            </a>
           </i>
           , a tie-in to the 2009
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_(film)" title="Star Trek (film)">
             <span style="cursor: help;" title="???">
              Star Trek
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           film, depicted Picard as having left Starfleet by 2387 to become the Federation Ambassador to
           <a href="/wiki/Vulcan" title="Vulcan">
            Vulcan
           </a>
           ; his image actually appears in the
           <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Official_Motion_Picture_Adaptation" title="Star Trek: The Official Motion Picture Adaptation">
            comic book adaptation
           </a>
           as part of a collage from
           <i>
            Countdown
           </i>
           used to depict Spock's mind-meld with the
           <a href="/wiki/James_T._Kirk_(alternate_reality)" title="James T. Kirk (alternate reality)">
            younger Kirk
           </a>
           . "
           <a href="/wiki/The_Q_Gambit,_Part_1" title="The Q Gambit, Part 1">
            The Q Gambit, Part 1
           </a>
           ", an issue of
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Ongoing" title="Star Trek: Ongoing">
             Star Trek: Ongoing
            </a>
           </i>
           , reveals Q visited Picard again to inform him of Spock's survival. Data, resurrected in
           <a href="/wiki/B-4" title="B-4">
            B-4
           </a>
           's body, succeeded him as captain of the
           <i>
            Enterprise
           </i>
           -E.
          </li>
          <li>
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_Online" title="Star Trek Online">
             Star Trek Online
            </a>
           </i>
           then established Picard's retirement to private life as occurring in 2402 when he settled in his ancestral home of
           <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
            France
           </a>
           .
          </li>
         </ul>
